  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="review_563226139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/563226139" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/563226139?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399162428" href="/book/show/18249281-the-infinite-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer563226139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7002793951469859007">I really LOVED <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16101128.The_5th_Wave__The_5th_Wave___1_' title='The 5th Wave (The 5th Wave, #1) by Rick Yancey' rel='nofollow noopener'>The 5th Wave</a>. I read it in the middle of my college exams and it was the only thing that kept me sane in between studying. The atmosphere was just right, the writing was engaging to me, and I thought each of the characters brought something important to the table. <b>Such love is hard to follow.</b><br/><br/>When I opened this book I was both excited and nervous. My expectations were so high that I knew it was dangerous. And, what can I say? I really needn't have worried. There is something so utt</span>
  <span id="freeText7002793951469859007" style="display:none">I really LOVED <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16101128.The_5th_Wave__The_5th_Wave___1_" title="The 5th Wave (The 5th Wave, #1) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The 5th Wave</a>. I read it in the middle of my college exams and it was the only thing that kept me sane in between studying. The atmosphere was just right, the writing was engaging to me, and I thought each of the characters brought something important to the table. <b>Such love is hard to follow.</b><br /><br />When I opened this book I was both excited and nervous. My expectations were so high that I knew it was dangerous. And, what can I say? I really needn't have worried. There is something so utterly compelling about Yancey's writing that makes me think we would be great friends in real life. <br /><br />This book has more flaws and not quite as much eerie atmosphere now the big secrets are out... but, overall, it is a worthy sequel that <b>didn't fail to punch me in the gut numerous times</b>. If you were a little worried that Yancey wouldn't be able to pull out another good 'un after <i>The 5th Wave</i> - don't be.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The world will burn for a hundred years. Fire will consume the things we made from wood and plastic and rubber and cloth, then water and wind and time will chew the stone and steel into dust. How baffling it is that we imagined cities incinerated by alien bombs and death rays when all they needed was Mother Nature and time.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I think the first book is a quieter novel, which had different effects on different readers. I, personally, thought it was one of the book's strengths. <i>The Infinite Sea</i>, however, is a different kind of book. We finished the first after a huge climax of action and drama; the secrets were out, covers had been blown, we were suddenly dropped into the middle of a war that only escalated with this second book. Here things go from bad to worse; people are lost, distrust lingers between the characters, these kids have had to grow up faster than kids ever should.<br /><br /><b>To get the negative out of the way...</b><br /><br />The most annoying thing about this book is Cassie. I am relieved that Yancey chose to write in a style that moves from perspective to perspective effectively because she might have driven me crazy otherwise. Yancey's characters are so different and have so many layers that I don't believe for a second that the author was chanelling his own beliefs through Cassie, but that didn't stop me from hating her slut-shaming and self-righteousness. <br /><br />Her love for Evan is a little more nauseating in this sequel than in the first, but I am glad that this whole situation introduces us to a minor but fascinating character called Grace. This is her from Cassie's perspective:<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“a tall girl with a cascade of honey-blond hair and striking Norwegian-model-type features, piercing blue eyes, full, pouty, collagen-packed lips, and the willowy figure of a runway fashion princess.<br />“Hello, Evan,” Cosmo Girl said. And of course her voice was deep and slightly scratchy like every seductive villainess ever conceived by Hollywood.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />*eye roll* and then later...<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Why don’t you tell me,” I shot back. “You extraterrestrial slut.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Allow me to point out that she is a "slut" because she used to be with Evan before Cassie came along. Cassie and Evan are like the Mary Sue and Gary Stu at the centre of this book who angst over each other with emo poetry. If these things bug you too you might be wondering how this book still manages to pull out a load of awesome and get a high rating...<br /><br />Because - and I should probably stress this - Cassie and Evan are only a very small part of <i>The Infinite Sea</i>. This book is full of different characters and interesting little back stories that it's easy to just ignore those two. As I said, we get to meet Grace who I found fascinating. We hear the back story between her and Evan so she becomes something more interesting and well-rounded than merely Evan's ex who is being used as a tool to make Cassie jealous. And we learn Poundcake's disturbing history and find out just why he never speaks.<br /><br />But my favourite character? <b>Ringer.</b> She was rapidly becoming my favourite in the first book and this one just cemented my love for her. I love everything about her. From the rage that bubbles beneath the surface:<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“My anger is greater than the sum of all lost things.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />To her flirtations with Zombie, her intriguing back story and the way she tells Cassie exactly how it is:<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Beats hanging around here waiting for your alien prince to come."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />In the end, this was a really good sequel with plenty of action, drama, twists and turns. I didn't reread the first book before I started and that didn't affect my enjoyment; I got sucked back into the world and story instantly. I feel like I'm just completely on the same wavelength as Rick Yancey because his writing always just <i>works</i> for me; he can be writing about action or characters or philosophical musings... and I genuinely enjoy reading it. <b>Can't wait for the next book.</b><br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7002793951469859007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1058069846" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1058069846" />
    <a title="NReads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34369915-nreads"><img alt="NReads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600781665p2/34369915.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1058069846?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NReads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NReads" href="/user/show/34369915-nreads">NReads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399162428" href="/book/show/18249281-the-infinite-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1058069846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8558382863001326188"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418789579ra/12894412.gif' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>____________________________________________<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“That’s the cost. That’s the price. Get ready, because when you crush the humanity out of humans, you’re left with humans with no humanity.<br/><br/>In other words, you get what you pay for, motherfucker” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>____________________________________________<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425928964i/13951955._SY540_.png' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>
  <b>Definitely not disappointing!</b>
</i><br/><br/><a href='http://geekybookie.tumblr.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>You can find the full review and more about this book on my blog!</a><br/><br/><p>
  <i>First I want to say something. Before reading this, I heard many many bad reviews and things about this </i></p></span>
  <span id="freeText8558382863001326188" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418789579ra/12894412.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>____________________________________________<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“That’s the cost. That’s the price. Get ready, because when you crush the humanity out of humans, you’re left with humans with no humanity.<br><br>In other words, you get what you pay for, motherfucker” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425928964i/13951955._SY540_.png" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>Definitely not disappointing!</b>
</i><br><br><a href="http://geekybookie.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">You can find the full review and more about this book on my blog!</a><br><br><p>
  <i>First I want to say something. Before reading this, I heard many many bad reviews and things about this book, and if you know me, you would know that The 5th Wave is my favorite dystopian of all time, and to be honest ,after hearing those things I kind of stepped away from this book because I didn't want it to "destroy" the first book as many people have said. Now I have read it, I don't understand all that hate. This is not a bad sequel, this is not bad at all. I know it is a little boring, but that's just in the beginning, and after that the story is really really interesting. And I know this is not as good as the 5th wave but it is not bad, it's actually really enjoyable read. So don't hesitate,you will like it.</i>
</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425928964i/13951956._SY540_.png" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>____________________________________________<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“When you look death in the eye and death blinks first, nothing seems impossible.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><p><i>The Infinite Sea</i> follow the story of the first book "The 5th Wave". Now after they know which is the 5th wave, they are being followed by the "Aliens". After they survived at the camp, they found a place to stay. Cassie is still waiting for Evan, and Ben and Ringer and the others are trying to find other survivors. Everything changes after Ringer gets captured and Evan comes.</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425928964i/13951957.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>____________________________________________<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It isn’t that the lies are too beautiful to resist. It’s that the truth is too hideous to face.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><p>To be honest I didn't like Ringer's POV. It felt like Cassie is not the protagonist anymore, and I really like her. Ringer is still a great character but still Cassie got my heart in the first book. Also Poundcake's POV was kind of pointless.</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425928964i/13951958._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>____________________________________________<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“People die. Love endures.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><p><i>The ending was spectacular</i>. Not as mind blowing as the first, but still Rick Yancey has a special ability for ending the books. So beautiful.</p><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425929118ra/13951966.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>____________________________________________<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Ha-ha. The dumb jock who can’t talk the Queen’s English. I swear to God, the next person who corrects my grammar gets punched in the face.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><p>Also <i>the writing style</i> is so unique. I really like it ,even that sometimes it gets a little complicated and it is hard to follow, but still so beautiful. Especially the Evan's POV is written perfectly.</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425929118i/13951967.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>____________________________________________<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“No hope without faith, no faith without hope, no love without trust, no trust without love. Remove one and the entire human house cards collapses.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><p>I highly recommend this book to every 5th Wave reader. It didn't disappoint me ,and it's a great sequel, believe me.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="8558382863001326188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_641015787" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/641015787" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/641015787?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=derp-moments">derp-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dragged-on-too-much">dragged-on-too-much</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=slut-shaming">slut-shaming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=good-but-not-great">good-but-not-great</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=second-book-syndrome">second-book-syndrome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer641015787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14676082862076614950"><b>*zero spoilers for the first book*</b><br/><br/>Good morning, The Infinite Sea. I'm afraid I have some bad news. You're suffering from a bad case of <b>Second Book Syndrome.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435632193ra/15366559.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It's a common affliction in the YA middle child. Symptoms include <b>dragging narrative, long periods of character inertia, lack of substantial plot, and padding.</b> While it's not contagious, people reading you may experience boredom or frustration. <br/><br/>There's no known cure, I'm afraid. You're going to have to wait it out. I'd advise a year long quar</span>
  <span id="freeText14676082862076614950" style="display:none"><b>*zero spoilers for the first book*</b><br><br>Good morning, The Infinite Sea. I'm afraid I have some bad news. You're suffering from a bad case of <b>Second Book Syndrome.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435632193ra/15366559.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's a common affliction in the YA middle child. Symptoms include <b>dragging narrative, long periods of character inertia, lack of substantial plot, and padding.</b> While it's not contagious, people reading you may experience boredom or frustration. <br><br>There's no known cure, I'm afraid. You're going to have to wait it out. I'd advise a year long quarantine--or longer--for your entire trilogy to come out. <br><br>You have also contracted <b>Slut-Shaming Pox</b>, a particularly nasty case, too. Also commonly seen in YA novels.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"...a tall girl with a cascade of honey-blond hair and striking Norwegian-model-type features, piercing blue eyes, full, pouty, collagen-filled lips, and the willowy figure of a runway fashion princess.<br><br>"Hello, Evan," Cosmo Girl said. And of course her voice was deep and slightly scratchy like every seductive villainess ever conceived by Hollywood."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>When your character encounters an enemy, it's best to dwell on more important matters, such as how to escape, rather than commenting on how her looks makes her a slut. ...Yes, yes, I'm sure you didn't mean it. Either way, I would recommend a strict diet of feminist works and a rehab stint at Tumblr or Goodreads. The people there will sort you out in no time.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435632193ra/15366560.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let's see, there was something else... Ah, yes, you have a mild bout of <b>Excess Symbolism Flu.</b> I was quite surprised; usually this disease shows up in overly pretentious works and badly-written ones. This sickness causes you <b>to bash readers over the head with hinting.</b> Not lethal, of course, but very annoying.<br><br>Your name is The Infinite Sea, and the phrase was mentioned multiple times in your body.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"...the one he carries across an infinite sea."<br><br>"...a stone around my neck to carry me down to the bottom of an infinite sea."<br><br>"I am drowning in an infinite sea."<br><br>"...an infinite sea of blood that envelopes me and bears me down to the lightless bottom."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>You can see how readers would feel <i>overwhelmed</i> if I may and irritated. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380974515ra/3623655.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then there's the matter of the rats living in the walls of the abandoned hotel your characters were living in, which were referenced almost religiously in the first several chapters. I had my suspicions then and then they were confirmed when the rats turned out to be an analogy for human-alien relations. <br><br>My advice: lay off the booze and treat your readers with respect. You'll be surprised by how intelligent most of them are. <br><br>And I believe we're done here. <b>Your writing is thriving</b>, by the way. Whatever you're doing, keep doing it. Follow my instructions regarding the afflictions I told you and you'll be right as rain in no time. Good day!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400446377ra/9677280.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14676082862076614950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review641015787">

  <span id="freeText10114822120477970903" style="display:none">The Infinite Sea (The 5th Wave, #2), Rick Yancey<br /><br />The Infinite Sea is a young adult science fiction novel written by American author Rick Yancey. The novel is the second in The 5th Wave trilogy, preceded by The 5th Wave and followed by The Last Star. <br /><br />After fleeing from a camp established by aliens, 16-year-old Cassie Sullivan, her brother and a squad of child soldiers attempt to prevent the extermination of the human race. <br /><br />A few days after the events of the first novel, Cassie, Ben, and the rest of squad 53 have taken refuge at a hotel, which they call "Walker Hotel" in honor of Evan Walker, who is thought to be dead after destroying Camp Haven. <br /><br />Ringer, believing that their refuge in the hotel will not last, goes out searching for a cave system mentioned on a brochure. Teacup, who she had grown close to, sneaks up to Ringer who shoots her, mistaking Teacup for a Silencer. A helicopter flies in and they are both captured by The Others.<br /><br />While Cassie and the others anxiously await Ringer, they realize that Teacup has gone missing, and Dumbo and Poundcake set out to find her but return empty-handed. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز شانزدهم ماه نوامبر سال 2015 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: سه گانه موج پنجم - کتاب دوم دریای بیکران؛ نویسنده: ریک (ریچارد) یانسی؛ مترجم: مهنام عبادی؛ مشخصات نشر تهران، نشر بهداد، 1393؛ جلد دو از سه، در 400ص، شابک 9786009554638؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 21م<br /><br />همین دو روز پیش روز آخر دیماه سال 1397خورشیذی دوباره خواندمش، بسیار سنگین است، شخصیتها را گم میکردم، چند روز پس از رخدادهای نخستین رمان، کاسی، بن، و بقیه در یک هتل پناه گرفته بودند، و بقیه رویدادها ...؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_1051711674" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1051711674" />
    <a title="Reading Teen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3329955-reading-teen"><img alt="Reading Teen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294347905p2/3329955.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1051711674?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Teen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Teen" href="/user/show/3329955-reading-teen">Reading Teen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1051711674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer711187602877816779">Why I DNF'd this book:<br/><br/>I am so sad that this book was such a disappointment.<br/><br/>I loved The Fifth Wave so much. I mean, 5-star-loved it! From beginning to end, that book had me captivated. So, you can imagine my disappointment when I finally decided . . .<br/><br/>I'm not finishing this book.<br/><br/>Excessive, redundant, unneeded, superfluous. These are the words that came to mind over and over as I was trudging through the first 2/3 of this book. I was just so bored. The first half of the book is filled with endless </span>
  <span id="freeText711187602877816779" style="display:none">Why I DNF'd this book:<br /><br />I am so sad that this book was such a disappointment.<br /><br />I loved The Fifth Wave so much. I mean, 5-star-loved it! From beginning to end, that book had me captivated. So, you can imagine my disappointment when I finally decided . . .<br /><br />I'm not finishing this book.<br /><br />Excessive, redundant, unneeded, superfluous. These are the words that came to mind over and over as I was trudging through the first 2/3 of this book. I was just so bored. The first half of the book is filled with endless musings about all the whys, whens and hows these "others" were trying to annihilate the humans. I don't mind this being a part of the story, but it just went on and on, and nothing else happened.<br /><br />I kept trying to push through.<br /><br />I felt like if I could just keep going a little while longer, it would get better. I had faith. But in the end, I just have too many other books that need read to waste my time on a book that I have to force myself to keep reading.<br /><br />In the end, I just didn't care anymore.<br /><br />The story dragged so much that I just lost interest in it. The characters felt flat to me, the mystery lost its appeal, and the romance just died. Romance? What romance?<br /><br />So I cheated.<br /><br />I knew my friend, Jen from Jenuine Cupcakes, had just finished, so I just asked her to tell me how it ended. Let me just tell you, I enjoyed her summarizing more than the actual book. And after hearing how it ended, I can't say I'm sorry I didn't finish it. (Double negative much?) I think if I had kept reading, I would have just been even more annoyed.<br /><br />In my opinion this was an unnecessary book.<br /><br />It was filler. The few important parts of this book could have been added to the other books, and it could have been an awesome duology. As it is, I don't know if I'll even have the motivation to read book 3.<br /><br />Dejectedly Yours, <br /><br />Andye<br /><a href="http://Readingteen.net" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingTeen.net</a><br /><br />Update: I did end up finishing this, I just let it play (audiobook) in the background while I did other things. The only way I got through this was because it was the audiobook (which was well done). The ending was so weird and anticlimactic! And again, just a complete waste of time. <br /><br />Content:<br /><br /> Profanity: Very Heavy<br /> Sexual Content: Heavy (but brief)<br /> Violence: Heavy</span>
  <a data-text-id="711187602877816779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1526516797" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1526516797" />
    <a title="Reading Corner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46088881-reading-corner"><img alt="Reading Corner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440473163p2/46088881.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1526516797?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Corner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Corner" href="/user/show/46088881-reading-corner">Reading Corner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1526516797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15106034939621532757">I definitely prefer <i>The Fifth Wave</i> to this book but <i>The Infinite Sea</i> doesn't fail to deliver and is an excellent sequel.The plot isn't as engrossing as the first book, due to the unveiled mystery but this book still manages to reel you into the unwinding chaos and takes hold of your emotions.<br/><br/>The writing is fantastic, as it submerges you into the catastrophe and fear the characters have to bear, in order to survive.The characters struggle is really felt in this novel, as all of the characters are</span>
  <span id="freeText15106034939621532757" style="display:none">I definitely prefer <i>The Fifth Wave</i> to this book but <i>The Infinite Sea</i> doesn't fail to deliver and is an excellent sequel.The plot isn't as engrossing as the first book, due to the unveiled mystery but this book still manages to reel you into the unwinding chaos and takes hold of your emotions.<br /><br />The writing is fantastic, as it submerges you into the catastrophe and fear the characters have to bear, in order to survive.The characters struggle is really felt in this novel, as all of the characters are put into sticky situations which make you question what you would do.<br /><br />More characters are explored in this book, like Poundcake and Ringer who is a real badass.I loved her pov and how her character develops as the story progresses.It was also interesting to get an insight into her and Poundcake, I really enjoyed it.However,I think Cassie and some of the others should have gotten more chapters because most of the characters are incredibly likeable and fun to read.<br /><br />Ringer's romance was cute and heart-breaking but I don't like all the inter-connecting love triangles,it's just a bit ridiculous.The idea of Cassie and Ben really grew on me and I found I was losing interest in Evan and Cassie being together,I don't think they match up as well.<br /><br />Overall, this is a great sequel to <i>The Fifth Wave</i> because of the beautiful writing which contains some fantastic quotes,the gripping plot and engaging characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15106034939621532757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1560030232" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1560030232" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582366251p2/21803154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1560030232?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781101996980" href="/book/show/25194192-the-infinite-sea">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Definitely Everyone.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=beautiful-stories">beautiful-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=great-fighting-scenes">great-fighting-scenes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=highly-recommend">highly-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=preciously-owned">preciously-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=movie-based">movie-based</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=will-reread">will-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=cliffhanger">cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1560030232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14995081652287605857"><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>Even the stars will wink out one by one and there will be no light or heat, and this is the war, the endless, futile war against the lightless, heatless void rushing toward us.</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br/><u>
  <b>[Impressive Reading Experience]</b>
</u><br/>Oh, wow, the most enjoyable thing while reading this is that I'm completely amazed by <b>how perfect and powerful <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3377941.Rick_Yancey' title='Rick Yancey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rick Yancey</a>'s words are.</b> He's indeed an extraordinary writer because he never fails to overwhelm you with seemingly simple descriptions yet you'll feel the strength a</span>
  <span id="freeText14995081652287605857" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>Even the stars will wink out one by one and there will be no light or heat, and this is the war, the endless, futile war against the lightless, heatless void rushing toward us.</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><u>
  <b>[Impressive Reading Experience]</b>
</u><br>Oh, wow, the most enjoyable thing while reading this is that I'm completely amazed by <b>how perfect and powerful <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3377941.Rick_Yancey" title="Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">Rick Yancey</a>'s words are.</b> He's indeed an extraordinary writer because he never fails to overwhelm you with seemingly simple descriptions yet you'll feel the strength and emotion beneath them at the same time. Reading both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16101128.The_5th_Wave__The_5th_Wave___1_" title="The 5th Wave (The 5th Wave, #1) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The 5th Wave</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16131484.The_Infinite_Sea__The_5th_Wave___2_" title="The Infinite Sea (The 5th Wave, #2) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Infinite Sea</a> is such a huge pleasure I seldom have so I can't stop praising how wonderful and flawless his writing style is. <br><br>Let's start with the story! Like the first book, this one contained alternative POVs from several characters in the story, but mostly from <b>Ringer's</b> instead of <s>my favorite</s> Cassie's. <br><br><u>
  <b>[Evan &amp; Cassie]</b>
</u><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"I found you, but in finding you, I lost myself."</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br>We know that Cassie and Evan seperated in the end of <i>The 5th Wave</i>, so <i>technically</i>, she was supposed to find him and he was supposed to keep his promise. However, life wasn't easy particularly in the alien-apocalypse era. As much as she wanted him to come back to her, her determination faltered with the passing of time, and her stress increased gradually. Predictably, Cassie's faith in him would more or less lost bit by bit when her "friends" didn't believe in her story about Evan Walker, so she began to doubt whether there was a real human inside him. Despite the struggle, she still managed to stay strong and put her big girl pants on. <blockquote>
  <b>I'd forgotten how cruel the Others could be. Not enough to punch a hole through my heart with a bullet. No, first you have to pummel it and stomp on it and crush it in your hands until the tissue oozes from between your fingers like Play-Doh.</b>
</blockquote><br>As for Evan, it's actually a relief to see him badly injured AND alive. He showed us that not all aliens downloaded in human bodies was unbreakable and perfect; some of them, like him, was wounded and <i>malfuntioned</i>, and by saying "malfuntioned", I mean not only his broken body, but also his mindset--the way he chose not to destroy humankinds as the commander ordered--was pinpointed as the ultimate target of Vosch(the commander), which brought out the next part of the story. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458362600i/18478948.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Honestly, the last chapter, DUBUQUE, surprised me most, because never did I expect Rick would end the story this way. The scene was so unbelievably beautiful and memorable; the characters might not appear perfect, but the combination of imperfections made it nothing to fastidious about.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458362600i/18478949.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>
  <b>[Ringer &amp; Razor]</b>
</u><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"Some things, down to the smallest of things, are worth the sum of all things."</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br>At first I disliked Ringer a lot because of her arrogant and pessimistic attitude toward everything she and her buddies had to face, and because she didn't believe whatever Cassie told of Evan. I even hated her because she was so proud of building up her own fortress and shutting people who cared about her out. And the way she thought pretending everything was fine could make her feel better when everything wasn't so at all. In my opinion, she was just avoiding the consequences and being an ostrich the entire time, but the more I knew about her, the less I felt this way. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458362600i/18478950._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>She went through a lot of experiments in the alien lab and I didn't like seeing her manipulated like a puppet. Even though she tried hard to fight back, it was apparently in vain. The products of the 5th wave always knew her next step <i>before</i> she took the initiative. So the time she met one of the soldiers, nicknamed <b>Razor</b>, in the building, she <s>fell for</s> punched him in the throat with all the strength she got. Yep, typical Ringer's style. Thankfully, they became friends afterwards. I mean, c'mon, he even played chess with her, umm, despite the fact that he didn't know how. <blockquote>
  <b>He opens the box, pulls out the board, fumbles with the pieces.<br>"You got your queens and kings and the prawns and these guard-tower-looking things. How come every piece is like a person except those?"<br>"<i>Pawns</i>, not <i>prawns</i>. A prawn is a big shrimp."<br>He nods. "That's the name of a guy in my unit."<br>"Shrimp?"<br>"Prawn. Never knew what the hell it meant."</b>
</blockquote><br>I'm glad Rick spent more chapters from Ringer's POV here or else I wouldn't get enough of them. They were adorable together and exchanged many funny banters whenever they chatted. The deeper they felt for each other, the more intimate they interacted. <blockquote>
  <b>He brought me from the tomb. He raised me from the dead. He risked his life so I might have mine. Easier to turn aside. Easier to let me go. Easier to believe the beautiful lie than the hideous truth. <br>"Now we're even," I whisper.<br>"Not exactly," he says hoarsely. "I only kissed you once."</b>
</blockquote><br>What made me extremely heartbroken was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the end of their just-the-beginning relationship. Was Razor really dead in the end? I mean, his chest was <i>blown apart</i>, which meant he was dead, right? I just couldn't wrap my head around that thought!!! Please someone tell me I misunderstood it. That I misinterpreted that phrase. *wailing* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>I felt like they were just started to know and explore each other but Razor already made his decision. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458362600i/18478951._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>
  <b>[The End]</b>
</u><br>This is such an impressive series and though I enjoyed the first book more than this one, <i>The Last Star</i> is still my most anticipated book of this year. I have a feeling Rick won't disappoint all of us and the ending must be both happy and bittersweet. The author gave us some space for imagination and rethink about the essence of humanity and I begin to ponder upon the meaning of the 5th wave, whether those aliens really occupied our bodies without being affected by their original hosts. It's getting philosophical <i>by the end of this trajectory that even Vosch failed to predict.</i> <b>Highly recommend this book to everyone!</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458362600i/18478952.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14995081652287605857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1094222383" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1094222383" />
    <a title="Dylan Williams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7023131-dylan-williams"><img alt="Dylan Williams" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587870270p2/7023131.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1094222383?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dylan Williams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dylan Williams" href="/user/show/7023131-dylan-williams">Dylan Williams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141345840" href="/book/show/16131526-the-infinite-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1094222383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17641897064181933409"><b>This books was a train wreck, and I really did not like it.</b> I read the 5th wave about a year ago, and whilst I didn't think it was anything special, I did enjoy myself while reading it. <i>This book</i> however, has all of the exact same problems just to far greater extremes. <br/><br/>Let's start with the basics; this books is a really poorly structured sequel. The story jumps straight back into where it left off in the 5th wave, without any refresher of who these people are, what they are doing, and what the p</span>
  <span id="freeText17641897064181933409" style="display:none"><b>This books was a train wreck, and I really did not like it.</b> I read the 5th wave about a year ago, and whilst I didn't think it was anything special, I did enjoy myself while reading it. <i>This book</i> however, has all of the exact same problems just to far greater extremes. <br /><br />Let's start with the basics; this books is a really poorly structured sequel. The story jumps straight back into where it left off in the 5th wave, without any refresher of who these people are, what they are doing, and what the point is. This was a serious problem considering the books were published a year apart. When I think of some of my favourite series (like Legend and Percy Jackson), what makes them so great is that each book reintroduces all you need to know so that you aren't confused - this book didn't do this. And for the first 100 pages or so I spent the whole time trying to reimagine the characters, and I was seriously confused. If you were reading this book straight after the 5th wave however, this wouldn't be much of a problem. <br /><br />On top of this, once I managed to figure out who everyone was and what the relationships were, I still wasn't enjoying myself because the way the characters interact and how they are developed is done so poorly that it was really irritating to read - there isn't a single character that I liked in this book. I found the points of view annoying and the supposed <i>romantic relationships</i> completely unrealistic and unbelievable.<br /><br />The thing that made the 5th wave most enjoyable for me was the plot, it was engaging and really intense. This book however, was completely pointless. The pacing of the book just really didn't work for me - It took so many pages to do absolutely nothing. It could have easily been compressed into about 100 pages and did not deserve its own book, and would have been far more enjoyable added to either the end of the 5th wave of the beginning of the next book in the series.<br /><br />Plus, I just really wanted <i>more</i>! I hate to compare it to the legend series again - but what I loved about those books is that it slowly expands the scope of the novel to introduce other parts of the world... This book however, with an apocalypse scenario that has supposedly devastated the planet, focuses far too directly on one character.<br /><br />The story did pick up a bit towards the end, and started to resemble the engaging plot that I remembered from the 5the wave - but it wasn't enough to redeem this book. I will not be continuing on with this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17641897064181933409" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Let's just say that this book, along with The 5th Wave, is one of my all time favorite books. It was so wonderfully, absolutely, magnificently amazing!!! I loved this book so much! It killed me to not be able to read this book for a week or so due to my homework and studies for school. Killed me. I've never taken as many honors classes as I have now, and one of my greatest regrets of that is losing time(like, all of it) for myself. But when I did get to read it, I fell in absolute love. My heart says Razor though, I think. Ben and Ringer was like a cute couple thing to me. Razor and Ringer, now that made me feel the feels, made my heart ache and hurt when they hurt and rejoice when they rejoiced. BUT THE ENDING. Freaking Razor. WHAT THE ACTUAL NUGGET?!?! You just sacrifice yourself? What duh what?! Uhhh NO. Nonononono. Right as you make me love you with Ringer, you probably like, DIE OR SOMETHING. *throws tantrum* NO! I liked you, dude! You were perfect for Ringer! Perfect! Stinkin' Rick and your stinkin' uncertainess and your stinkin' mysteriousness and your stinkin' CLIFF HANGERS. Ugh.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7517034691756864863"><b>*4.25 SILENT STARS*</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"People die. Love endures."</i>
</b><br/><br/>I didn't love this book as much as I loved the prequel, but it was pretty <i>enjoyable</i> nonetheless!<br/>By the way, I completely forgot I still had to write this review, oops! Basically, most of what happened in this one was everyone getting their bearings and it felt like more of an extremely long prequel to the third book, which I honestly can't wait to read.<br/><br/>Though the first half of this book was pretty <i>boring</i>, the second part was seriously <i>awe-inspiri</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7517034691756864863" style="display:none"><b>*4.25 SILENT STARS*</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"People die. Love endures."</i>
</b><br /><br />I didn't love this book as much as I loved the prequel, but it was pretty <i>enjoyable</i> nonetheless!<br />By the way, I completely forgot I still had to write this review, oops! Basically, most of what happened in this one was everyone getting their bearings and it felt like more of an extremely long prequel to the third book, which I honestly can't wait to read.<br /><br />Though the first half of this book was pretty <i>boring</i>, the second part was seriously <i>awe-inspiring</i> yet again. I have no clue where Rick Yancey gets his inspiration for all these crazy plot twists, but <b>boy</b> I love it! The last few chapters had me going crazy yet again!<br /><br />I loved that this book involved a lot of Ringer's POV, since we didn't get that in the previous one. My love for her has increased exponentially (just like my love for Evan tbh). Cassie was sassy and badass as always, no surprise there! We also got to learn a lot more about everyone's past and that's part of what makes these books so interesting. <br /><br />I still haven't seen the movie of the first book, but since I read that it doesn't have very good ratings, I'm quite sad that they're probably not gonna turn this one into a book as well. <br />I seriously can't wait to have the third and probably final book in this trilogy in my hands, because I expect it to be <b>one hell of a ride</b>!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<span id="freeTextContainer6886612860900526418">The good news everyone is dying for: NO LOVE TRIANGLE. In fact, there's hardly a romantic component to this book at all. <br/><br/>If anything there is <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ a love triangle with Ringer and another soldier instead of Ben. But that's just going with my definition. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>And there's no cliffhanger! Not rea</span>
  <span id="freeText6886612860900526418" style="display:none">The good news everyone is dying for: NO LOVE TRIANGLE. In fact, there's hardly a romantic component to this book at all. <br /><br />If anything there is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ a love triangle with Ringer and another soldier instead of Ben. It all depends on your definition of love triangle. To me, no. The tryst with the other soldier is clearly a one time ordeal. And Ringer and Ben were never that much of a couple anyway. But that's just going with my definition. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And there's no cliffhanger! Not really. Nothing nowhere near as bad as The Fifth Wave. Hooray.<br /><br />This volume was a bit disorienting to read. The first 2/3 cover a span of just a day or two. The final third covers a period of about a month and sticks with just one character whereas the first 2/3 have a consistent and even POV switch.<br /><br />It is almost entirely nothing but action. And while it was a very enjoyable read and I was riveted, I really missed the emotional impact of the first book. There's practically no time for character development in the ensuing chaos. I hope Book 3 will more than make up for it.<br /><br />Also, there <i>are</i> some intriguing developments in what we learn about the Others and what their ultimate goal is but far more questions are raised than answered. I guess that's par for the course for a middle book. <br /><br />Rick Yancey's writing is as solid as ever, though. We're fully poised for an explosive and gutwrenching finale.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6886612860900526418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1059205461" />
    <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters"><img alt="Trina (Between Chapters)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530495507p2/9323164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1059205461?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trina (Between Chapters)" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters">Trina (Between Chapters)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399162428" href="/book/show/18249281-the-infinite-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1059205461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18150653229163721538"><b>Reread in May 2016.<br/>Rating:</b> 3.5 stars because I keep wavering between 3 and 4.<br/><b>Updated review:</b><br/>In my original review (below) I said this book felt like filler and didn't advance the plot much. Upon rereading, I actually disagree with my previous statements. Reading the first 2 books back to back gave me a much bigger picture. And again, the story follows the same pattern as the first book by having one group on the outside, and one group on the inside of the whole alien operation, which I feel lend</span>
  <span id="freeText18150653229163721538" style="display:none"><b>Reread in May 2016.<br />Rating:</b> 3.5 stars because I keep wavering between 3 and 4.<br /><b>Updated review:</b><br />In my original review (below) I said this book felt like filler and didn't advance the plot much. Upon rereading, I actually disagree with my previous statements. Reading the first 2 books back to back gave me a much bigger picture. And again, the story follows the same pattern as the first book by having one group on the outside, and one group on the inside of the whole alien operation, which I feel lends a great amount of harmony to the story.<br /><br />It also worked better as a reread because knowing what to look for allowed me to catch on to more things. So, I enjoyed this more than I did the first time, but it's not as strong as the first book, mainly due to it's short length and time period covered. I don't think it's useless filler, but I am wondering what on earth Yancey has planned for the finale.<br /><br /><b>First read in October 2014.<br />Original review:</b><br />I don't feel like much progress was actually made in this story, it felt like all filler.<br /><br />What went wrong for me was that we spent so much time watching our characters set things up only to never see it play out. Especially with the plan they formed just fizzling out. I just don't understand the motives behind writing it that way. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I'm referring to how Evan gives Cassie the map and the bomb and tells her that if she goes to Grace's house the Mothership will send a pod down to collect Grace, but Cassie can send the bomb up in the pod instead and blow the Mothership to smithereens. But then Sam loses the bomb and Poundcake uses it to blow up the hotel to take out Grace. Seems to me like using it on the Mothership instead of on one Other (especially when Evan was sacrificing himself to try to take her out) would have been a better plan.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> True, this plan may not have worked, but why even bring it up if he knew it wouldn't happen? Filler.<br /><br />In the last section we do learn something new about the Others, which was pretty cool, and something happens to a character which can turn the tables and take the story in a new direction, but again, we just get pages and pages of filler describing games of chess and eye colors instead of doing anything with these new plot developments and then the book just ENDS.<br /><br />Plus, the thing that we do learn feels sort of like Yancey was trying to back track, or didn't know how to pull off what he had originally set up. Or, more likely, not enough time was spent exploring this new information. The book was very short and so much of the word count was spent retelling the same scenes or describing how many broken bones someone had at any given time instead of on the characters really processing much of anything.<br /><br />Honestly, the important information could have been added into The 5th Wave, or the next book. There was just very little build up and very little pay off.<br /><br />Luckily, The 5th Wave was so good that it was still good to read anything about this world. But I can't help but wonder if book 3 will be a big let down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18150653229163721538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_887861734" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer18067380771459362158">This is an alien invasion, right? And if you had any doubts after reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16101128.The_5th_Wave__The_5th_Wave___1_' title='The 5th Wave (The 5th Wave, #1) by Rick Yancey' rel='nofollow noopener'>The 5th Wave</a> just how far these beings out of time and space will go in search of dominion over this planet and its indigenous occupants, the opening chapter of The Infinite Sea will <s>erase</s> blast those doubts into smithereens. It grabs you by the throat and whispers wetly in your ear…..”Listen Up Chump!” <br/><br/>We pick up with Cassie right where book one ended. She’s got Sams, with his bedraggled bear, as well as Zombie and the re</span>
  <span id="freeText18067380771459362158" style="display:none">This is an alien invasion, right? And if you had any doubts after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16101128.The_5th_Wave__The_5th_Wave___1_" title="The 5th Wave (The 5th Wave, #1) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The 5th Wave</a> just how far these beings out of time and space will go in search of dominion over this planet and its indigenous occupants, the opening chapter of The Infinite Sea will <s>erase</s> blast those doubts into smithereens. It grabs you by the throat and whispers wetly in your ear…..”Listen Up Chump!” <br /><br />We pick up with Cassie right where book one ended. She’s got Sams, with his bedraggled bear, as well as Zombie and the rest of Ben’s ragtag group, waiting with mounting impatience for Evan. Where in hell is he or as Ringer might say, “What to hell is he?”<br /><br />The focus here is not so much on Ben and Cassie or even Evan for that matter. Instead we learn more about that ragtag squad of Ben’s, most notably Ringer. That is not to say the rest of them are ignored, in fact we do learn more about Evan’s earlier (pre invasion) days, which is how we meet Grace. This is Cassie’s first impression:<br /><br /><i>Dumbo was back in the doorway, slack-jawed, red-eared, and in the grasp of a tall girl with a cascade of honey-blonde hair and striking Norwegian-model-type features, piercing blue eyes, full, pouty, collagen-packed lips, and the willowy figure of a runway fashion princess.<br />“Hello Evan” Cosmo Girl said. And of course her voice was deep and slightly scratchy like every seductive villainess ever conceived by Hollywood.</i><br /><br />Yancey gets an A plus for this character. I loved her.<br /><br />But back to Ringer, following her and learning more about this rigid, void of feeling, unsmiling girl will lead the reader to a better, okay I’m just going to say, <u>understanding</u> of what is really going down here.<br /><br />Maybe, hard to know for sure, when you’re riding a paradigm shifting wave……..Woot!<br /><br />I am holding on for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16131489.The_Last_Star__The_5th_Wave___3_" title="The Last Star (The 5th Wave, #3) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Star</a> Mr. Yancey.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18067380771459362158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_924040271" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/924040271" />
    <a title="Leahxx" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25510442-leahxx"><img alt="Leahxx" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435517019p2/25510442.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/924040271?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leahxx" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leahxx" href="/user/show/25510442-leahxx">Leahxx</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer924040271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13201852382700882881">So basically at first I was like, "Eh, this book is pretty mediocre compared to the first." And then as the book progressed I was like, "HOLY COW THIS BOOK IS FABULOUS." So yeah, I am completely and 100% in love with this book. I mean is it better than the first one? Hard to say, but they're pretty close. <br/><br/>!!!!!!!! SPOILERS. !!!!!!!<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>1. Wow, so Razor? Yeah, I want one. How is it that all these super attractive and amazing guys are surviving this apocalypse? I would really love to know. Because if t</span>
  <span id="freeText13201852382700882881" style="display:none">So basically at first I was like, "Eh, this book is pretty mediocre compared to the first." And then as the book progressed I was like, "HOLY COW THIS BOOK IS FABULOUS." So yeah, I am completely and 100% in love with this book. I mean is it better than the first one? Hard to say, but they're pretty close. <br /><br />!!!!!!!! SPOILERS. !!!!!!!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />1. Wow, so Razor? Yeah, I want one. How is it that all these super attractive and amazing guys are surviving this apocalypse? I would really love to know. Because if this is how it's going to be during a real apocalypse, I say bring it on. Anyway, I adore him and Ringer. That was so perfect and we're going to forget the betrayal part, minor detail, minor detail. We are also going to forget the part where he gets shot in the chest. That didn't happen. <br />2. If Ringer is going to cling onto her feelings for Razor and Cassie refuses to stop being in love with Evan, WHO IS GOING TO END UP WITH BENJAMIN PARISH, THE BOY WHO STOLE MY HEART. I personally enjoy fantasizing about him and Cassie, but clearly we aren't headed down that road. He had better end up with someone though because he can't die and he can't be alone. Well he can be alone if it means he's not dead. <br />3. POUNDCAKE. WHY. HE WAS ONE OF MY FAVORITES. HE WAS SO ADORABLE. That made me so sad. He was so brave though. It makes me sad that no one ever really understood him. <br />4. So are we saying that it isn't an alien apocalypse now? That it's just a bunch of crazy intelligent, horrific human beings making it seem like an alien apocalypse? My mind is completely fried from that realization in the book. <br />5. At first I didn't think I'd like the Ringer POV and I dreaded reading that huge section that was hers, but it was actually so insanely good. I have so much more respect for her and I genuinely like her character now. <br />6. Cassie is forever one of my favorite main characters because she's so sassy and I don't know, she's just great. But sometimes I would enjoy punching her in the face because of how she fails to handle <br />certain situations, but she's under a lot of pressure. I get that. <br />7. I like this book a lot because it's about so much more than just survival and love and regular story crap like that. There are so many deep thinking parts, like how Vosch asks Ringer all those questions and how no one ever knows who to trust and there are so many crazy twists and turns. I love it. <br /><br />Overview- the next one needs to be in my hands by tomorrow or I might have a meltdown, but this may be hard to accomplish because we have no idea when the next one is supposed to be released haha. Just wow. I need to stop and contemplate life for the next few hours, so this review is finished. Bye.</span>

<div id="review_1056408325" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1056408325" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5376236-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595863428p2/5376236.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1056408325?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/5376236-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5376236-heather?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1056408325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7405669823554268464">I was patiently waiting for this book all year. If your not new to my Youtube channel, then you will know how much I LOVED The 5th Wave. I thought it was amazingly written, creepy and I just fell in love hard with it. So it's safe to say I had huge expectations for the sequel.<br/><br/>It didn't meet them though to me.<br/>The first problem I have with it is that it's 160 pages shorter than the first book. Granted the first book isn't an insanely long book, it clocks in at 460 pages but to have a sequel only 3</span>
  <span id="freeText7405669823554268464" style="display:none">I was patiently waiting for this book all year. If your not new to my Youtube channel, then you will know how much I LOVED The 5th Wave. I thought it was amazingly written, creepy and I just fell in love hard with it. So it's safe to say I had huge expectations for the sequel.<br /><br />It didn't meet them though to me.<br />The first problem I have with it is that it's 160 pages shorter than the first book. Granted the first book isn't an insanely long book, it clocks in at 460 pages but to have a sequel only 300 pages long? Not cool! <br /><br />I felt like the first half of this book could have easily been a novella. There wasn't much that went on and it drug on for that matter. I loved reading Cassie &amp; Evan's part but Ben was really annoying in this book. I just wanted to punch him quite honestly. <br /><br />I was surprised about the POV's in this book. In the first book we do get mutiple POV's but mostly it's from Cassie. In this book I would say 70% of the book follows Ringer...which if I'm honest I didn't hate.<br /><br />I didn't love at first that it was mainly Ringer's POV because I just wanted to read more Cassie..more Evan but I gotta say I liked the change of pace. Ringer's part in the whole book was the most interesting and it gripped me the most because the first half of the book was so ehhhh.<br /><br />Ringer is a complex character. She is abrasive, tough and hard to read but man is she fun to read. I loved reading all her parts and her struggle in this book was REAL. <br /><br />The last 50 pages kinda made up for this book but not completely. Like I said the first half of the book was just ok and I think could have been cut but the second half was pretty good!<br /><br />I didn't hate this book by any means, I just thought it would be a tad more epic. <br />I am hoping the last book will be AMAZING &amp; answer all of our many questions and just be rock solid.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7405669823554268464" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17530236137410266857" style="display:none"><b>4 STARS</b><br /><br />PLOT - 4<br />CHARACTERS - 4<br />WRITING STYLE - 3.5<br />ROMANCE - 3<br />UNPUTDOWNABLE LEVEL - 4<br /><br />It's as <b>amazing</b> as the first book but I'm only giving it 4 stars because I don't feel like it flowed well. There were so many stories going on in so many directions and coming together messily. It's still intense, still brilliantly awesome, but sadly it's lacking in appeal.<br /><br />I wouldn't say I'm disappointed, I loved it but at the same time I'm aware that this book wasn't a <i>very</i> strong installment in the trilogy. My feelings for this series remains unchanged, though, and I'm still looking forward to reading the final book! <br /><br /><b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BAuys8IqPcHhtcgPxCZNvKp6FLTDO/PO2L9cQximbzE+LdtheXT0qUaefG4z00djfCXzfA22famDwRry1eWdqw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('b3JzD8G3KqZp/5Q6/oKB4paE0SVqFyboFrHu5Lk9Z5JVVBrdeunjzs7UIFsJd4s9QNs27aSaqI9Nz6hVdH6VCA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer8455282751174982255">aka Richard Yancey<br/><br/>Rick is a native Floridian and a graduate of Roosevelt University in Chicago. He earned a B.A. in English which he put to use as a field officer for the Internal Revenue Service. Inspired and encouraged by his wife, he decided his degree might also be useful in writing books and in 2004 he began writing full-time.<br/><br/>Since then he has launched two critically acclaimed series: The Ext</span>
  <span id="freeText8455282751174982255" style="display:none">aka Richard Yancey<br /><br />Rick is a native Floridian and a graduate of Roosevelt University in Chicago. He earned a B.A. in English which he put to use as a field officer for the Internal Revenue Service. Inspired and encouraged by his wife, he decided his degree might also be useful in writing books and in 2004 he began writing full-time.<br /><br />Since then he has launched two critically acclaimed series: The Extraordinary Adventures of Alfred Kropp, for young readers, and The Highly Effective Detective, for adults. Both books are set in Knoxville, Tennessee, where Rick lived for ten years before returning to Florida. </span>
